
		          CONFIGURATION FILE FOR VERITAS at the basecamp
			      Configuration Sept 2009 to July 2012
			     (after T1 move, before camera upgrade)
		       =====================================================

				 DETECTOR FILE FOR GRISUDET

====================================================================================================

Changes 11/27/2012 (GM)

1) changed low to high gain ratio from 6 to 5.0

Changes 10/18/2012 (CS)
1) changed distance of adjacent pixels from 31.0mm to 31.4mm

Changes 04/23/2012 (AB)

1) Gain values increased by 7.5% to match the gain increase found when going from 20 samples readout window to 32 samples. See this presentation for details: http://veritas.sao.arizona.edu/wiki/images/0/09/GainUncert_2012Jan.pdf.
2) New 1pe pulse defined over 64ns (to match the gain measurement taken over 32 samples, see item 1)). See this elog for details: http://veritas.sao.arizona.edu/private/elog/AnalysisAndCalibration/2386.
3) New trigger threshold: T1, T2, T3 => 66mV; T2 => 64mV. New values were derived from this analysis: http://veritas.sao.arizona.edu/wiki/index.php/Study_of_L1_trigger_threshold. GrisuDet now accepts different trigger thresholds for different telescopes:
4) Shift MC trace position by 2 samples to better match the pulse trace position in our data. See this Elog: http://veritas.sao.arizona.edu/private/elog/AnalysisAndCalibration/2387

Changes 10/27/2011 (LR)

1) Use new Quantum efficiency curve provided by Nepomuk after the Montreal meeting (average Curve)
2) Use new reflectivity curves from Jeff but add an extra efficiency factor so that the integral of 
the reflectivity curve reflects the relative gain of the telescope.  T1, T2, T3, T4 = 0.93, 0.81, 1.0, 0.95
3) For PMPIX flags we set all PMT efficiencies to 1. Since we will not be using this feature anymore 
to set the relative gains between telescopes.
4) Changed ANLOG current gain from 1.975e5 to 1.910e5 to reflect the 5.3 dc/pe ratio that has been 
for new array. The previous radio reflected 5.48 dc/pe ratio which was the measured value for T1
(other telescopes were normalized to T1 via the PMPIX flag)
5) New mirror alignment values (MIREL flag). Using config values from Jeff circa Jun 5, 2011

Changes 06/11/2010 (BH)

1)  FADCS pedestal changed from 20 to 16 to better match data (on average).
2)  PMPIX single-pe amplitude fluctuation changed from 0.35 to 0.44, which 
    is the ~mean value for out PMTs (though they have a fairly large spread and
    tail towards high fluctuations).
3)  PULSE is updated again, to use the 0.5-ns sampling that matches
    the average measured pulse shape (measured Apr 2010). 
4)  PMPIX geometrical efficiency is set to 1.0 and PMT effective radius to 
    14.0 (net increase in effective area of PMTs of 5% over 15/10/2010 config).
5)  QUEFF curve updated. Between 310 and 650 nm, using the shape of the XP2960
    curve as measured by HESS and normalized to match measurements of our
    XP2970 PMTs made by UCSC and WashU at 450 and 500 nm. Between 180 and 300
    nm, using the same curve as previously used, which already agrees
    remarkably well in normalization with the UCSC/WashU measurements. See 
    http://veritas.sao.arizona.edu/wiki/index.php/GrisudetSimulationParameters
6)  TRIGG telescope coincidence time changed from 40ns to 50ns, default for
    observations.

Changes 15/10/2010

1)  mirror degradation restored to 1.0 (was 0.92 in earlier "best guess" configuration) since
    shadowing is now accounted for in optics simulation.
2)  updated PULSE to use an 0.5-ns sampling (earlier "best guess" used 2-ns sampling).
3)  dc/pe ratios set by looking at Nov 2009 data.
4)  mirror reflectivity set by looking at aging of mirrors - see
    http://veritas.sao.arizona.edu/private/elog/AnalysisAndCalibration/1503
5)  light cone efficiency increased by 5%
6)  thresholds set to 70 mV to account for neglecting DC offset, RFB, gain path difference factor
    (1.14).

Changes 23/09/2009

i) change noise settings in SIMUL and FADCS in accordance to Peter Cogan's old veritas4bc_pc_vegas_2.cfg

Changes 19/09/2009

i)   updated mirror misalignment values according to new PSF
ii)  CFG threshold changed from 50 mV to 35 mV

====================================================================================================

Changes 22/07/2009

i) added telescope 5 as new telescope 1 (new telescope position, Summer 2009)

ii) adjusted rotation point to corsika simulations

Configuration file for December 2007 simulations

Changes compared to June 2007 simulations

i) rotated mirrors by 90 deg (see mail by C.Duke)

ii) changed PSF to 0.07 deg

iii) dead channels according to run 38064 (Crab, 20071118)

iv) bug fix: dynamic range of FADC is 1530

v) set low gain multiplier according to low gain analysis results from 200712 (new line LOWMULT, used in eventdisplay only)

vi) set CFD threshold to 50 mV

vii) new mirror reflectivities according to measurments on 2007/11/26 (VBC elog 4395)

i) introduce true height if telescopes


====================================================================================================
Configuration file for September 2006 simulations

Changes (compared to standard grisudet configuration files):

i)   adjusted trigger thresholds taking different gains in CFDs and FADCs into account
             single PMT threshold is 55mV, but CFDs and FADCs different
             gain (factor is 1.2): 55 mV x 1.2 = 66 mV

ii)  sample length 24

iii) corrected PST patch 33, was wrong in originately distributed configuration file

iv)  PSF of 0.11deg

v)   Mirror reflectivity according to ELOG 103

vi)  PMT quantum efficiencies from John Finley's new measurements (ELOG 99)

vii) effective PMT radius of 12.3mm

viii)FADC digital output dynamic range of 2048 (account for overflows in analysis)

ix)  single pe rise/fall time according measurements

x)   Light cones crudely included 
     (JH) effective tube radius of 12.3mm (mean of ~20 values) measured by Purdue
     (JH) Assume 100% geometrical efficiency over this area, then 50% out to 15.5mm
     (JH) gives overall efficiency of 81%. This is a guess.

xi)  use 3-FOLD PST and 55mV CFD threshold

xii) changed single pe amplitude fluctuations to 0.35 (from 0.45, see calibration memo)

xiii)new telescope coordinates with origin in array center

* VERSN 4.2.0

Numbre of telescope (NBRTL)
* NBRTL 4

Telescope location in the field (TLLOC) the parameters are:
   -the telescope identification number 
   -the X (oriented towrd east) location cordinate in meters. 
   -the Y (oriented toward north)location cordinate in meters. 
   -the Z (oriented toward up) location cordinate in meters. 
   -the telescope rotation offset in meters.
	The telescope rotation offset is the distance below the focal point
        of the mirror along the optical axis about which the telescope
        rotates. (intersection of the elevation and azimuth axis)
   -the pointing offset in the x direction
   -the pointing offset in the y direction

coordinates August 2006, origin in array center for old array (origin offset 
for new array!)
Z coordinates set to zero for compatibility with Corsika; may want nonzero 
values with full grisu chain.

* TLLOC 1     135.48 -8.61 12.23.0 12.0 0.0 0.0
* TLLOC 2      44.1 -47.7 4.4 12.0 0.0 0.0
* TLLOC 3      29.4  60.1 9.8 12.0 0.0 0.0
* TLLOC 4     -35.9  11.3 7.0 12.0 0.0 0.0

The simulation parameter record SIMUL contains
   -the time between samples in ns (this is also the sampling time 
	for the simulation calculation to be carried with.)
   -the number of samples over which the simulation produces the signals
   -the number of samples over which the noise database is produced
(GM) should be 20000, but noise calculation currently extremly slow
* SIMUL 2.0 100 4000

The FADC record (FADC) contains
   -the FADC output ON-OFF status  (1=ON, 0=OFF)
   -the FADC output voltage per digital count in mV
   -the FADC pedestal in digital counts
   -the FADC digital output dynamic range
   -the number of sample to be written on the output for each channel.
   -the number of samples between the trigger and the beginning of the
	FADC record. A positive number corresponds to a record starting
	at a time anterior to the trigger time.
   -the number of samples in pedestal event records
   -The ratio between high and low gain for system with hi-lo gain switch
	dynamic range extention. If this number is less than 1.0 the function 
	is disabled. 
   -The threshold in FADCdigital counts for the low gain activation. 

(GM) noise length should be 20000, but noise calculation currently extremly slow
* FADCS 1 7.84 16.0 255 20 5 4000 5.0 250



The trigger record (TRIG) contains 
   -the telescope identifier
   -the single PMT threshold in mV
   -the discriminator output pulse width in ns
   -the pixel coincidence time window in ns
   -the minimum number of triggered channels required by the coincidence logic
   -the minimum number of telescopes required 
   -the telescope coincidence time window width in nanosecondes 
   -a flag which when set to 1 activates forced triggering. Non triggering
   telescopes are then read out while when the flag is at 0 they are not.
       Note:For the last three parameters, since they are specific to the 
            array and not to one particular telescope it is the values  
            entered for telescope 1 that are taken into account. 

(LR) single PMT threshold is 50mV, but CFDs and FADCs different
(LR) gain (factor is 1.14): 50 mV x 1.2 = 60 mV

* TRIGG 1 66.0 10.0 5.0 3 2 50.0 1
* TRIGG 2 64.0 10.0 5.0 3 2 50.0 1
* TRIGG 3 66.0 10.0 5.0 3 2 50.0 1
* TRIGG 4 66.0 10.0 5.0 3 2 50.0 1

Pattern Selection trigger (PSTON).
   -the minimum number of adjacent triggered channels required by the 
    pattern trigger logic
   -the number of 19 pixel trigger patches
* PSTON 3 91

Trigger patch list records (PATCH)
   -Patch identification number 
   -A flag indicating if the patch is enabled (1) or not (0).
   -List of id numbers for pixels in patch (0 indicates no pixel connected)
    The order of the 19 pixel list is important.
(GM) corrected patch 33 here, was wrong in originately distributed configuration file

The analog electronics record (ANLG) contains 
   -the PMT current gain
   -the equivalent system impedance(i.e. the conversion factor in Ohm
	between amps on the output of the PMT and voltages on the 
	output of the analog signal processing)
   -the electronics  voltage noise standard deviation in mV

Mirror design (MIROR). The parameters are 
   -the telescope identification number
   -the mirror radius in meters
   -focal length in meters
   -the focusing error in meters (>0 when camera is too 
	far away from the dish)
   -the mirror type (1=DavisCotton) 
   -the number of mirror elements. 

* MIROR 1 7.0 12.0 0. 1 357
* MIROR 2 7.0 12.0 0. 1 357
* MIROR 3 7.0 12.0 0. 1 357
* MIROR 4 7.0 12.0 0. 1 357

Mirror reflectivity curve (RFCRV). The flag is followed by 
   -the the reflectivity curve identification index 
   -the number of points given on the quantum efficiency spectral curve. 
This is followed by a serie of 
   -wave length(in nano-meter)
   -reflectivity(fraction of unity)

Mirror element (MIREL) characterisation. For each we have 
   -the telescope identification number
   -the mirror element identification number
   -the element shape (1=circular, 2=hexagonal, 3=square)
   -orientation angle(degrees). If 0.0, polygon side perpendicular
    to y-axis of the telescope coordinate system.
   -the external radius 
   -the curvature radius 
   -the x position of the element on the dish (in meters)
   -the y position of the element on the dish (in meters)
   -the maximum mis-alignement in degrees
   -the maximum blur radius in degrees
   -the degradation factor (1.0=perfect 0.0=missing)
   -the reflectivity curve identifier

(LR) New PSF model from Jeff circa Jun 5 2011

Quantum efficiency (QUEFF). The flag is followed by 
   -the quantum efficiency identification index 
   -the number of points given on the quantum efficiency spectral curve. 
This is followed by a series of lines giving 
   -wave length(in nano-meters)
   -quantum efficiency(fraction of unity) 
If the number of points is in excess of the indicated number, the last
values will be ignored. If the number of points lines is less than the
indicated number the remaining points will adopt the last value from the
list. Quantum efficiency data should be given before being refered to by
PMT characteristics. If quantum data are given twice for the same
quantum efficiency identification index, the second occurence will be
used in the simulations.

Camera design (CAMRA).
   -telescope identification number
   -the number of phototubes.
* CAMRA 1 499 0.0 1.0

Phototubes (PMPIX). For each we have 
    -the telescope identification number
    -the pixel identification number
    -the pixel shape (1=circular, 2=hexagonal, 3=square)
    -orientation angle(degrees). If 0.0, polygon side
     perpendicular to the y-axis
     -the X position coordinate in the focal plane in mm
     -the Y position coordinate in the focal plane in mm
     Camera coordinates are such that increasing X corresponds to
     going WEST when telescope is pointing SOUTH. Increasing Y
     corresponds to increasing elevation.
     -the PMT Radius in mm
     The PMT radius really is the radius of the sensitive area (Radius of
     the light cone input for example).
     -the geometrical efficiency which may be used to include the effects
     of light cone loss.
     -the quantum efficiency identification number to be used for that tube.
     -the single photoelectron signal relative amplitude fluctuation.
     -the signal rize time in nanosecondes
     -the signal fall time in nanosecondes
     -the RC coupling time constant in nanosecondes
     Note that the pulse shape can also be specified by a table. For this see instructions at the end of this file.
     -the bellongin of the channel to the trigger (1 if it bellongs,
     0 other wise)
     -a flag indicating if the pixel should be used in the analysis(1) or not(0)
     -a time offset in nanosecond. It measures how late the pulse is locate in
     the stack for each channel. the analysis and the simulation search
     for the smalles non negative value and subtract it from all the other
     to apply a relative correction.
     -a relative gain factor to account for the imperfect gain flat fielding.
     In the anlysis, each pixel value is multiplied by this number while
     in the simulation pulse amplitudes are divided by this number.



(JH) effective tube radius of 12.3mm (mean of ~20 values) measured by Purdue
(JH) Assume 100% geometrical efficiency over this area, then 50% out to 15.5mm
(JH) gives overall efficiency of 81%. This is a guess.

(GM) single pe values (amplitude fluctuations, rise and fall times)
(GM) according to calibration note from Jamie and Gernot (ELOG 720)
